<Text>The place is in a shopping center, on 8th St. Though, it may be easy to miss. It's not necessarily marketed all in your face. From the outside, it appeared to be this hole in the wall, amongst a various Filipino businesses. Nevertheless, the place was bigger than I thought. I got the No. 1. The broth wasn't bad, just seemed a little heavier than most. And the price isn't bad too. For the price of a small, you get what others may call a large.  And I typically ask for extra tripe, but I didn't can that much extra. < userid>
100477287364747733045< /userid>
< review>
I'm giving this four stars, honestly, out of nostalgia. And hope.  This was, at one point, a lovely theater. That time has long since passed.  There's been a few changing of hands in the last couple decades and it's now owned by what I believe is a non-profit preservation society.  Which is for the best. This isn't an IMAX theater.  It's an ooold theater. But old in the best way, with velvet curtains around the screen, crazy comfortable seats and bathrooms so old the lettering is in an art deco font.

I've seen some great movies here: Pulp Fiction, The Nightmare Before Christmas, The Dark Knight, and the greatest movie ever made: Raiders of the Lost Ark.  (It even had a teaser trailer for REVENGE of the Jedi!) The side building even used to be my favorite comic book shop!  So yeah, nostalgia plays a big part here.  But it is lovely. And I honestly believe that some day it'll be the five stars I want it to be.<//review>

< Review>
Pretty good ice cream shop and different ice cream experience. I love many topping options they have to get creative with. Granted it can be quite daunting to see all the choices, but they have a very clear step-by-step menu to help you through the process and build your ice cream. They are fairly expensive treats though. We got two mediums and the total came out to $15+. I wanna say this is one of the only rolled ice cream places here, so it's worth checking out at least once. It's definitely a good place to go to if you wanna spoil yourself.</Review>

<review>Hey yall! Have you tried #howweroll in #downtownvisalia ?! If not you absolutely should, locally owned and operated, and absolutely delicious. They let me get some action shots, and watch them assemble my ice cream right before my eyes! Fun for kiddos, and with summer around the corner ice cream is a great outing üòãüç¶Me and hubby tried Strawberry feild and Dirt worms, and oh boy was it good!
The ice cream lasted a good while in my cup and didn't melt as quick as one would anticipate. The ice cream its self takes Maybe 3 minutes to form and to freeze up and its a pretty awesome sight to see your ice cream being made right in front of you! I can't imagine all the fun combinations you could make if you added in your own mix ins and toppings.
Super clean inside and they had two little tables outside to enjoy your icecream as well. The two people making the ice cream whom I assume to be father and daughter were super friendly and kind. There is a whole printed list of combinations if you don't want to make your own which I have included down below, if your like me and need to study your choices before going!<//review>< Pics>

4< /rating>
<text>Nice little rolled ice cream shop in downtown Visalia. My girlfriend and I had ordered the monkey business (Nutella mixed with banana) and cookies and dreams (cookies and cream) in kid sizes. Which I think is perfect, I'm not a huge fan of ice cream but you get a good amount of ice cream for the $6 price we paid for each bowl. Customer service is good, friendly staff and the ice cream itself was average in my opinion. I've been to other rolled shops in LA and the Bay Area those were much better in creativity but I love the concept that is brought here to the sleepy area of the South Valley. As a restaurant owner myself I see so much potential here and I hope these folks do well along with improve on their creativity with their products. I know with COVID everything has been tough on everyone.  Overall it's a nice place to stop by for ice cream, if you never had rolled ice cream come by and try it; all while at the same time you're supporting a local business during these hard times. Flavor wise it was good but it wasn't enough to want me coming back for more, but then again I'm not really an ice cream guy.<//text><pics>None</pics><resp>None</resp><GmapID>0x80952fd09b150621:0x51dda69e24062827</GmapID></record></dataset><record>

< review>
It has seen better days.

I *tried* to love this place - I honestly did - but...

It certainly has "history."  It is an older restaurant in an older building, and the decor certainly reflects that.  The homemade tortillas are wonderful, but deceptively massive - they will fill you up before you finish your food!

I've lived in California and in New Mexico, so I feel qualified to say there a spectrum for carnitas - on one end they are crisp and dried out, and on the other they are very flabby and soggy.  I prefer crisp and juicy.  This place (on this day) pegged out the flabby and soggy end.  My wife's chicken enchilada was meat and red sauce on one of those massive tortillas.  The sauce was flavorful, but uninteresting.

The menu prices are more in line for an upscale restaurant in a part of town with more,,, cach√©.  Caveat emptor.< /review>

<Review>I am from Minneapolis where we have our fair share of authentic Mexican restaurants (1st, 2nd, and 3rd generation immigrants in Minneapolis vs. a long-established Mexican population in California) and have been to this place 3 times now on my visits out to the Bay Area.  Some of THE BEST I have ever had--these guys are the real deal.  Their tortillas are homemade and unlike anything I have ever tasted, but in a good way - YUM!  Here's a hint:  their chili verde isn't on the menu, but they will give it to you if you ask for it--to die for.  One of my best friends is from Hayward and he always asks for chili verde whenever we have gone - the server recognizes him and always comments on how he orders the same thing every time.  I will definitely go back!<//Review>< Pictures>

<userid>108234321229646131832<//userid><Name>Brandon Williams</Name>< Date>
1594326353064<//Date>
<Rate>5<//Rate>< Review>
I was driving around looking for someone to help me during this COVID-19 situation. I went to Best Buy, the Apple Store, all these different places and they would always play the same card on me "sorry but because of the virus we basically can't do anything and we have become a crippled mass of flesh."

The virus is basically an easy and simple "out" for everyone to be like "sorry, but we're useless during this time and you just need to deal with it."

But not Di-No Computers...

I called over there and they ACTUALLY PICKED UP THE PHONE WITH NO RECORDED MESSAGE. Right away I was shocked. Who does that?

Then they helped me over the phone and invited me to drive over. WHAT?!

Then I got there and the guy was like "I looked for the phone and I couldn't find it, I'm so sorry." - then he went back and looked again and came out and said "oh hey, look I found a phone."

I had a pin on and he was curious about what it was and asked me about it. They are genuinely super nice and interested in you as a person.

Honestly, I'm not so sure I have ever been to a place with such lively staff. One of the guys started talking to me about a computer he was fixing that was a fossil and I asked why someone would fix something like that. He mentioned it was because people run super expensive computer programs and it's tens of thousands of dollars to upgrade the software. It was incredible.

The staff were friendly and laughing and joking and you could tell they get A LOT of repeat business. WELL I KNOW WHY.

The place was hot and their product supply was in disarray but this place was ONE-HUNDRED PERCENT CUSTOMER SERVICE ORIENTED.

COVID is not an excuse to be worthless and you can still help people and do your job during this time. A situation like COVID is where the children are separated from the adults, the amateurs separate from the professionals.

But you can tell it was just another day in the office. They weren't doing something "special."

Honestly, if an office is looking to find a local place to take their staff to show them a live demonstration of how customer-service should be, this might be a great place to take them.

We got our new phone with one signature and a smile.

I'm still shocked. Can't recommend this place enough.< /Review>

<name>Mark Mayer<//name><Gmap_id>0x80c2dcabc55fd4bd:0x476f32c23f4739f8<//Gmap_id><Text>I had a horrible experience with Di-No in the early 2000s.  I had a G4 Tower with a faulty power button. I did my research and saw that a few others had had this problem, and that it was a circuit board that was part of the button mechanism. I even found the part #. I took it in to Domino Computing in Pasadena, CA, explained the problem, gave them the part #, and they said they'd have a look at it. A few days later, they reported it was the motherboard, which they'd be happy to replace for me for $800 parts and labor. I asked if they had tried to troubleshoot the power button or its circuit board. No, they hadn't, but they were sure because they were Apple Certified Technicians and I wasn't.

Now the kicker. Since I turned down their repair, I had to pay a $50 diagnostic charge to get my computer back. After an hour of getting nowhere, i.e., waiting for different people to deign to come down to the floor and tell me "no", I finally paid up. Driving home, I happened to notice a computer repair place with a small Apple sticker in the window. I stopped there, and they were able to order the part, which was around $100. Installing it for me would be $20, or I could save the money if I wanted to do it myself. The process was described as trivial, and it was.

< review>
Went to Moon Valley to buy a whole slew of trees/plants for our backyard. Lacey helped us find trees for our project - she did a great job finding trees I was specifically looking for (even looking at other Moon Valley locations) and showing me trees I hadn't thought of. She was very patient and never rushed us, even though we wanted to see a lot. I made some changes to the order before the delivery day and she was always accommodating and quick to respond (really quick!).

Delivery and planting day went well. Brandon, Juan, Alex and Manuel were all pros. They planted about 30 trees and plants and were excellent about consulting with me about placement and right before trees went into the ground (to choose best face) - trees were all straight and placed in exactly the right spots. There was no question that they knew exactly what they were doing.

My only advice if you're ordering a lot of plants is to choose/approve EVERY plant before delivery day - there were a few plants that were much too small for their price/container size, which we cancelled - but it was all taken care of with no problem. I wouldn't hesitate to buy from them again - especially trees.<//review>

I am a big fan of TJ Maxx and this is my favorite location. Everytime I go in, I am always coming out with more stuff that I needed. Their inventory is amazing. My greatest finds at this location have been Hydroflasks, Rae Dunn items, Le Creuset cookware, Kate Spade, Lucky Brand jeans, Addidas shoes, Joe Jeans, perfumes, Michael Kors clothing, healthy snacks, facial masks, Shiseido & Estee Lauder skincare products, organic shampoo/conditioner, etc (all for a fraction of the price of regular retail shops).
